style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;text-decoration:underline;">Results of Operations and Financial Condition</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">On July 23, 2015 we issued a press release announcing our results of operations for the second quarter and six-month period ended June 30, 2015, including, among other things, income statements for those periods.  In addition, on the same day we held a teleconference for analysts and media to discuss those results.  The teleconference was web cast on our web site.  The press release and related financial statements are attached to this Form 8-K as </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;text-decoration:underline;">Exhibit 99.1</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-bottom:16px;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">In our press release, we use non-GAAP financial measures, such as non-GAAP net income and earnings per share, that differ from financial statements reported in conformity to U.S. generally accepted accounting principles (&#8220;GAAP&#8221;).  Our non-GAAP financial measures adjust our reported results to exclude the impact of significant acquisitions and divestitures, including amortization of intangible assets primarily associated with costs of marketed products acquired or licensed from third parties.  We also exclude other items that are typically highly variable, difficult to predict, and of a size that could have a substantial impact on our reported operations for a period.  We believe that these non-GAAP measures provide useful information to investors. Among other things, they may help investors evaluate our ongoing operations.  They can assist in making meaningful period-over-period comparisons and in identifying operating trends that would otherwise be masked or distorted by the items subject to the adjustments.  Management uses these non-GAAP measures internally to evaluate the performance of the business, including to allocate resources and to evaluate results relative to incentive compensation targets. </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Investors should consider these non-GAAP measures in addition to, not as a substitute for or superior to, measures of financial performance prepared in accordance with GAAP.  For the reasons described above for use of non-GAAP measures, our prospective earnings guidance is subject to adjustment for certain future matters, similar to those identified above, as to which prospective quantification generally is not feasible. </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">The information in this Item&#160;2.02 and the press release attached as Exhibit&#160;99.1 are considered furnished to the Commission and are not deemed filed for purposes of Section&#160;18 of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended. </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">compared with the second quarter of 2014. The revenue growth included increases of </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">8</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#160;percent due to increased volume and </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">1</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#160;percent due to higher prices, largely offset by a decrease of </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">8</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;percent due to the unfavorable impact of foreign exchange rates. The </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">8 percent</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;increase in volume was primarily due to the inclusion of revenue from Novartis Animal Health, and to a lesser extent increased volume for several products, including Cyramza and Trulicity. These worldwide volume increases were partially offset by lower demand for Cymbalta</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;"><sup style="vertical-align:top;line-height:120%;font-size:pt">&#174;</sup></font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;and Evista</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;"><sup style="vertical-align:top;line-height:120%;font-size:pt">&#174;</sup></font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">, largely due to U.S. patent expirations in December 2013 and March 2014, respectively. Revenue in the U.S. increased </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">6</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#160;percent to </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$2.528&#160;billion</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">, driven primarily by higher prices, the inclusion of revenue from Novartis Animal Health and increased volume for several products, partially offset by patent expirations for Cymbalta and Evista. Revenue outside the U.S. decreased </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">4</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#160;percent to </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$2.451 billion</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">, driven by the unfavorable impact of foreign exchange rates, partially offset by the inclusion of revenue from Novartis Animal Health and increased volume for the majority of pharmaceutical products, due in part to wholesaler buying patterns in Japan.</font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">Gross margin remained relatively flat at </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$3.760 billion</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;in the second quarter of 2015, as the favorable impact of foreign exchange rates on international inventories sold and the inclusion of Novartis Animal Health were largely offset by the foreign exchange impact on revenue and inventory step-up and amortization costs. Gross margin as a percent of revenue was </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">75.5 percent</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">, a decrease of </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">0.4</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;percentage points compared with the second quarter of 2014. The decrease in gross margin percent was primarily due to the inclusion of Novartis Animal Health and inventory step-up and amortization costs, largely offset by the impact of foreign exchange rates on international inventories sold.</font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">Operating expenses in the second quarter of 2015, defined as the sum of research and development and marketing, selling and administrative expenses, were </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$2.805 billion</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">, a decrease of </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">2</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#160;percent compared with the second quarter of 2014. Research and development expenses decreased </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">2 percent</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">to $1.169 billion, or </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">23.5 percent</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;of revenue, driven primarily by the favorable impact of foreign </font></div><br><div><div style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;in the second quarter of 2015, compared with </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">22.0 percent</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;in the second quarter of 2014. The decrease in the 2015 effective tax rate was primarily due to the tax impact of the net charge related to the repurchase of debt, acquired in-process research and development charges, and asset impairment, restructuring and other special charges. The 2015 effective tax rate also reflected a net discrete tax benefit of approximately $24&#160;million. Neither period includes the benefit of certain expired U.S. tax provisions, including the R&amp;D tax credit. </font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">In the second quarter of 2015, net income decreased </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">18</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#160;percent to </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$600.8 million</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">, and earnings per share decreased </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">18</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;percent to </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$0.56</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">, compared with </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$733.5&#160;million</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;and </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$0.68</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">, respectively, in the second quarter of 2014. The declines in net income and earnings per share were driven by charges related to the repurchase of debt and lower operating income, partially offset by a lower effective tax rate. </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><a name="s3490F067747822204E3E20AE3BB473E5"></a><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;text-decoration:underline;">Second-Quarter 2015 Non-GAAP Measures</font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">On a non-GAAP basis, worldwide revenue was </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$4.979 billion</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;in the second quarter of 2015, a decline of </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">4</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#160;percent compared with the second quarter of 2014. The revenue decline was driven by the unfavorable impact of foreign exchange rates and lower demand for Cymbalta and Evista following U.S. patent expirations, partially offset by increased volume for several products, including Cyramza and Trulicity, and higher prices. U.S. revenue increased </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">3 percent</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$2.528&#160;billion</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">, driven primarily by higher prices and increased volume for several products, partially offset by the patent expirations for Cymbalta and Evista. Revenue outside the U.S. decreased </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">11 percent</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$2.451 billion</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">, driven by the unfavorable impact of foreign exchange rates, partially offset by increased volumes for the majority of pharmaceutical products.</font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">Gross margin decreased </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">1</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;percent to </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$3.945&#160;billion</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;in the second quarter of 2015, as the negative impact of foreign exchange rates on revenue was largely offset by the favorable impact of foreign exchange rates on international inventories sold and increased volume. Gross margin as a percent of revenue was </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">79.2</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;percent, an increase of </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">2.5</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;percentage points compared with the second quarter of 2014. The increase in gross margin percent was due to the impact of foreign exchange rates on international inventories sold.</font></div><br><div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:10pt;"><div to </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$1.600&#160;billion</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">, due to the favorable impact of foreign exchange rates, cost reductions in the combined animal health organization and ongoing cost-containment measures, partially offset by marketing and selling expenses related to new product launches. style="vertical-align:bottom;border-bottom:1px solid #666666;padding-left:2px;padding-top:2px;padding-bottom:2px;padding-right:2px;"><div style="overflow:hidden;height:24px;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#160;</font></div></td></tr></table></div></div></div><br><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">of U.S. patent exclusivity in March 2014. Sales outside the U.S. </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">decreased</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">14 percent</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$46.0 million</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">, driven by the unfavorable impact of foreign exchange rates.</font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;text-decoration:underline;">Animal Health</font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">In the second quarter of 2015, worldwide animal health sales totaled </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$840.8 million</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">, an increase of </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">40</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#160;percent compared with the second quarter of 2014. U.S. animal health sales increased </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">24 percent</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$410.0 million</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">, and animal health sales outside the U.S. increased </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">60 percent</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">$430.8 million</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">. The increases were primarily driven by the inclusion of revenue from Novartis Animal Health.</font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">Including the sales of Novartis Animal Health in 2014, worldwide animal health sales decreased </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">4</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;percent, U.S. animal health sales increased </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">1</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;percent and animal health sales outside the U.S. decreased </font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">9</font><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">&#32;percent. The increase in U.S. animal health sales was driven by increased volume in companion animal products and to a lesser extent higher prices, partially offset by decreased volume in food animal products. The decrease in animal health sales outside the U.S. was driven by the unfavorable impact of foreign exchange rates, partially offset by increased volume, primarily in food animal products, and to a lesser extent higher prices. Including the sales of Novartis Animal Health in 2014 and excluding the unfavorable impact of foreign exchange rates, worldwide animal health sales increased 3 percent.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><a name="s9B58FF243F7664F7163D20AE65241661"></a><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:bold;text-decoration:underline;">2015 Financial Guidance</font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:6pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:6pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:12pt;">The company has revised certain elements of its 2015 financial guidance on a reported basis and on a non-GAAP basis. Full-year 2015 earnings per share are now expected to be in the range of $2.20 to $2.30 on a reported basis. On a non-GAAP basis, full-year 2015 earnings per share are now expected to be in the range of $3.20 to $3.30.</font></div><div style="line-height:180%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:10pt;">(a)</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:10pt;">The company uses non-GAAP financial measures that differ from financial statements reported in conformity with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles (GAAP). The company's non-GAAP measures adjust reported results to exclude items that are typically highly variable, difficult to predict, and of a size that could have a substantial impact on the company&#8217;s reported operations for a period. Non-GAAP adjusted amounts for 2014 assume the Novartis Animal Health acquisition was completed on January 1, 2014. Beginning in 2015, non-GAAP financial measures for periods presented also exclude amortization of intangibles primarily associated with costs of marketed products acquired or licensed from third parties. The company believes that these non-GAAP measures provide useful information to investors. Among other things, they may help investors evaluate the company&#8217;s ongoing operations. They can assist in making meaningful period-over-period comparisons and in identifying operating trends that would otherwise be masked or distorted by the items subject to the adjustments. Management uses these non-GAAP measures internally to evaluate the performance of the business, including to allocate resources and to evaluate results relative to incentive compensation targets. Investors should consider these non-GAAP measures in addition to, not as a substitute for or superior to, measures of financial performance prepared in accordance with GAAP. style="width:48px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;padding-left:24px;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:10pt;">(a)</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:Garamond,serif;font-size:10pt;">The company uses non-GAAP financial measures that differ from financial statements reported in conformity with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles (GAAP). The company's non-GAAP measures adjust reported results to exclude items that are typically highly variable, difficult to predict, and of a size that could have a substantial impact on the company&#8217;s reported operations for a period. Non-GAAP adjusted amounts for 2014 assume the Novartis Animal Health acquisition was completed on January 1, 2014. Beginning in 2015, non-GAAP financial measures for periods presented also exclude amortization of intangibles primarily associated with costs of marketed products acquired or licensed from third parties. The company believes that these non-GAAP measures provide useful information to investors. Among other things, they may help investors evaluate the company&#8217;s ongoing operations. They can assist in making meaningful period-over-period comparisons and in identifying operating trends that would otherwise be masked or distorted by the items subject to the adjustments. Management uses these non-GAAP measures internally to evaluate the performance of the business, including to allocate resources and to evaluate results relative to incentive compensation targets. Investors should consider these non-GAAP measures in addition to, not as a substitute for or superior to, measures of financial performance prepared in accordance with GAAP.
